# What's new in Microsoft Fabric? archive

This archive page is periodically updated with an archival of previous year's content from [What's new in Microsoft Fabric?](whats-new.md)

To follow the latest in Fabric news and features, see the [Microsoft Fabric Blog](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/). Also follow the latest in Power BI at [What's new in Power BI?](/power-bi/fundamentals/desktop-latest-update?tabs=powerbi-service)

## Generally available features

The following table lists the features of Microsoft Fabric that have transitioned from preview to general availability (GA).

|**Month** | **Feature** | **Learn more** |
|:-- |:-- | :-- |
|April 2026|**Tabbed multitasking and object explorer (Generally Available)**|[Tabbed multitasking and object explorer (Generally Available)](https://community.fabric.microsoft.com/t5/Fabric-Updates-Blog/Fabric-April-2026-Feature-Summary/ba-p/5176490) deliver fully supported tabs for working across multiple Fabric items in parallel, plus an object explorer that browses items across open workspaces. The GA release adds right-click tab management, open-in-new-window, a resizable explorer pane, support for opening monitoring jobs as tabs, and accessibility improvements. For more information, see [Multitask with tabs and object explorer](./fabric-home.md#multitask-with-tabs-and-object-explorer).|
|April 2026|**Eventstream SQL operator (Generally Available)**|[Eventstream SQL operator is generally available](https://community.fabric.microsoft.com/t5/Fabric-Updates-Blog/Simplify-Real-Time-Pipelines-with-the-Fabric-Eventstreams-SQL/ba-p/5171983), the production-ready code-first transformation operator in Fabric Eventstreams, with multiple destinations from a single operator (Eventhouse, Lakehouse, Activator, downstream Eventstreams), built-in per-output testing in the canvas, and event-time processing with configurable late-arrival and out-of-order thresholds. For more information, see [Process events using a SQL operator](../real-time-intelligence/event-streams/process-events-using-sql-code-editor.md).|
|April 2026|**Nested folders support in shortcut transformations (Generally Available)**|[Nested folders support in shortcut transformations (Generally Available)](https://community.fabric.microsoft.com/t5/Fabric-Updates-Blog/Nested-folders-support-in-shortcut-transformations-Generally/ba-p/5171995) extends the zero-ETL shortcut transformations model to multi-level folder hierarchies with recursive change detection, automatic partition pickup, directory structure preservation, and a single Delta table output per top-level folder. The Include subfolders option is enabled by default for new and existing transformations. For more information, see [Shortcuts file transformations](../onelake/shortcuts/transformations.md).|
|April 2026|**Outbound access protection for Data Factory (Generally Available)**|[Workspace outbound access protection (OAP) for Data Factory (Generally Available)](https://community.fabric.microsoft.com/t5/Fabric-Updates-Blog/Outbound-access-protection-for-Data-Factory-Generally-Available/ba-p/5172006) extends workspace-level outbound controls to Pipelines, Copy Job, Dataflows, and Mirrored Databases (including Mirrored SQL Database and Mirrored Snowflake), so Data Factory items in a protected workspace only connect to admin-allowed endpoints. For more information, see [Workspace outbound access protection overview](../security/workspace-outbound-access-protection-overview.md) and [Workspace outbound access protection for Data Factory](../security/workspace-outbound-access-protection-data-factory.md).|
|April 2026|**Cross-workspace logging for MLflow in Microsoft Fabric (Generally Available)**|[Cross-workspace logging for MLflow (Generally Available)](https://community.fabric.microsoft.com/t5/Fabric-Updates-Blog/Cross-workspace-logging-for-MLflow-in-Microsoft-Fabric-Build/ba-p/5172000) lets you log MLflow experiments, metrics, parameters, and registered models from any environment (Fabric notebook, Azure Databricks, Azure Machine Learning, local) to any Fabric workspace via the `synapseml-mlflow` package and the `MLFLOW_TRACKING_URI` environment variable, enabling dev/test/prod MLOps separation and train-where-data-lives, serve-from-a-separate-workspace patterns. For more information, see [Cross-workspace logging for MLflow in Microsoft Fabric](../data-science/machine-learning-cross-workspace-logging.md).|
|April 2026|**Fabric Local MCP (Generally Available)**|[Fabric Local MCP (Generally Available)](https://community.fabric.microsoft.com/t5/Fabric-Updates-Blog/Agentic-Fabric-How-MCP-is-turning-your-data-platform-into-an-AI/ba-p/5172009) is the open-source on-machine Model Context Protocol server that gives AI assistants grounded knowledge of Fabric's APIs, OneLake file operations, and Fabric item operations with integrated authentication, error handling, auto-retry, and telemetry, and works with VS Code GitHub Copilot, Cursor, Claude Desktop, and any MCP-compatible client. The Fabric Remote MCP server is also available as a preview feature. For more information, see [Get started with Fabric Pro-Dev MCP Server](/rest/api/fabric/articles/mcp-servers/pro-dev-local/get-started-local).|
|April 2026|**Warehouse ALTER TABLE support in an explicit transaction (Generally available)**|Supported `ALTER TABLE` Transact-SQL operations can now execute inside an explicit user-defined transaction in Fabric Data Warehouse. For more information, see [Transactions in Fabric Data Warehouse](../data-warehouse/transactions.md#explicit-transactions).|
|April 2026|**Shortcut transformations (Generally Available)**|[Shortcut transformations](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/shortcut-transformations-and-turn-files-into-delta-tables-without-pipelines-generally-available?ft=All) automatically turn structured files into Delta tables as you bring data into or move it within OneLake, keeping data always in sync without the need for pipelines. For more information, see [Shortcuts file transformations](../onelake/shortcuts/transformations.md).|
|March 2026|**Sensitivity labels in Fabric public APIs (Generally Available)**|[Sensitivity labels in Fabric public APIs (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/sensitivity-labels-in-fabric-for-public-apis-generally-available?ft=All) expose sensitivity label metadata through List Items, Get Item, and Update Item API responses, enabling programmatic classification monitoring, AI agent guardrails, and compliance automation. For more information, see [Sensitivity Labels in Fabric and Power BI](../governance/protected-sensitivity-labels.md).|
|March 2026|**Scheduled job failure notifications (Generally Available)**|[Scheduled job failure notifications (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/get-notified-when-scheduled-jobs-fail-in-fabric-generally-available?ft=All) send email alerts when scheduled runs of Pipelines, Notebooks, Dataflows Gen2, and other Fabric items fail, with error details and a link to the failed run in the Monitoring Hub. For more information, see [Job Scheduler documentation](https://aka.ms/ScheduledJobNotifications).|
|March 2026|**Microsoft JDBC Driver for Fabric Data Engineering (Generally Available)**|The [Microsoft JDBC driver for Fabric Data Engineering (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/microsoft-jdbc-driver-for-microsoft-fabric-data-engineering-generally-available?ft=All) enables secure JDBC connectivity to Spark SQL workloads in Fabric via Livy APIs, providing native access to Lakehouse data in OneLake with enterprise Microsoft Entra ID authentication, built-in connection pooling, and compatibility with common JDBC tools and BI clients. For more information, see [Microsoft JDBC driver for Fabric Data Engineering](../data-engineering/spark-jdbc-driver.md).|
|March 2026|**PowerShell model for gateways (Generally Available)**|The [PowerShell module for gateways (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/powershell-module-for-gateways-with-expanded-automation-capabilities-generally-available?ft=All) delivers production-ready automation for gateway lifecycle, update, restore, and configuration management with new commands for version discovery, targeted updates, and gateway restoration. For more information, see [PowerShell support for on-premises data gateways](/data-integration/gateway/service-gateway-powershell-support).|
|March 2026|**New Dataflow Gen2 capabilities at FabCon Atlanta 2026**|[New Dataflow Gen2 capabilities](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/a-wave-of-new-dataflow-gen2-capabilities-at-fabcon-atlanta-2026?ft=All) include ADLS Gen2 and Lakehouse Files destinations (GA), relative references for portable dataflows (GA), email alerts for failed refreshes, scheduled runs with parameters, [Save as Dataflow](../data-factory/migrate-to-dataflow-gen2-using-save-as.md#save-a-dataflow-gen1-as-a-new-dataflow-gen2-cicd), and previews for Snowflake and Excel file destinations, diagnostics download, publish-time destination checks, and the Execute Query Streaming API. For more information, see [Dataflow Gen2 overview](../data-factory/dataflows-gen2-overview.md).|
|March 2026|**Fabric variable libraries in Dataflow Gen2 with CI/CD (Generally available)**|[Fabric variable libraries](/fabric/cicd/variable-library/variable-library-overview) offer a centralized way to manage configuration values across Microsoft Fabric workloads. With [integration in Dataflow Gen2](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/dataflow-gen2-variable-library-integration-in-microsoft-fabric-generally-available?ft=All), you can reference these variables directly in your dataflow, enabling dynamic behavior across environments and simplifying CI/CD workflows. For more information, see [variable libraries in Dataflow Gen2](../data-factory/dataflow-gen2-variable-library-integration.md).|
|March 2026|**Materialized Lake Views (Generally Available)**|[Materialized Lake Views (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/materialized-lake-views-in-microsoft-fabric-generally-available?ft=All) replace hand-built ETL pipelines with declarative Spark SQL or PySpark statements, adding multi-schedule support, broader incremental refresh, PySpark authoring, in-place updates, and data quality constraints. For more information, see [Get started with materialized lake views](../data-engineering/materialized-lake-views/get-started-with-materialized-lake-views.md).|
|March 2026|**Copy job watermark column types (Generally Available)**|[New watermark column types in Copy job (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/incremental-copy-gets-more-flexible-new-watermark-column-types-in-copy-job-in-fabric-data-factory-generally-available?ft=All) add **rowversion**, **date**, and string (interpreted as **datetime**) watermark support for incremental copy, enabling more flexible change tracking across SQL, date-based, and string-stored timestamp systems. For more information, see [What is Copy job in Data Factory?](../data-factory/what-is-copy-job.md).|
|March 2026|**Fabric Spark Applications Comparison (Generally Available)**|The [Spark Applications Comparison feature](../data-engineering/spark-comparison-runs.md) lets users select and compare up to four Spark application runs side by side. |
|March 2026|**Fabric Spark Diagnostic Emitter (Generally Available)**|The [Fabric Apache Spark Diagnostic Emitter](../data-engineering/spark-diagnostic-emitter-overview.md) allows Apache Spark users to collect logs, event logs, and metrics from their Spark applications and send them to various destinations, including [Azure Event Hubs](../data-engineering/azure-fabric-diagnostic-emitters-azure-event-hub.md), [Azure storage](../data-engineering/azure-fabric-diagnostic-emitters-azure-storage.md), and [Azure log analytics](../data-engineering/azure-fabric-diagnostic-emitters-log-analytics.md).|
|March 2026|**Fabric CLI v1.5 (Generally Available)**|[Fabric CLI v1.5 (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/fabric-cli-v1-5-is-here-generally-available?ft=All) adds one-command workspace deployments with fabric-cicd integration, first-class Power BI scenario support, pre-installed CLI in Fabric Notebooks, an AI agent execution layer, and Python 3.13 support. For more information, see [Fabric CLI documentation](https://microsoft.github.io/fabric-cli/).|
|March 2026|**Private link support for API for GraphQL (Generally Available)**|[Private link support for API for GraphQL (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/34710?ft=All) enables tenant-level private endpoint connectivity for GraphQL APIs, ensuring data traffic flows through Microsoft's private backbone network for enhanced security and compliance. For more information, see [About Private Links for Secure Access to Fabric](../security/security-private-links-overview.md).|
|March 2026|**Self-service workload publishing (Generally Available)**|[Self-service workload publishing (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/fabric-extensibility-self-service-workload-publishing-generally-available?ft=All) lets ISV partners publish custom workloads to up to 20 customer tenants for testing, reserve globally unique workload names, and run automated validation before pursuing formal certification in the Workload Hub. For more information, see [Publishing overview](../extensibility-toolkit/publishing-overview.md).|
|March 2026|**Workspace IP firewall rules (Generally Available)** | [Workspace IP firewall rules](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/workspace-level-ip-firewall-rules-in-microsoft-fabric-generally-available?ft=All) let workspace admins define an allow list of public IP addresses or IP ranges that can access a Fabric workspace, helping limit inbound access to approved network locations. For more information, see [Protect workspaces by using IP firewall rules](../security/security-workspace-level-firewall-overview.md).|
|March 2026|**ANY_VALUE aggregate function (Generally Available)**|The [`ANY_VALUE` aggregate function (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/use-any_value-for-simpler-grouping-of-results-in-fabric-data-warehouse-generally-available?ft=All) returns a representative value from each group without requiring it in the GROUP BY clause, simplifying queries when descriptive columns are functionally dependent on the grouping key. For more information, see [ANY_VALUE (Transact-SQL) function](/sql/t-sql/functions/any-value-transact-sql?view=fabric&preserve-view=true).|
|March 2026|**Fabric Data Agent (Generally Available)**| Create, configure, publish and share data agents that answer natural-language questions over data sources like Lakehouse, Warehouse, Semantic Models, Eventhouse, SQL Databases, and Mirrored Databases. Additional capabilities like troubleshooting using diagnostics, and CI/CD for end-to-end lifecycle management are also generally available. To learn more, see [Fabric Data Agents](../data-science/concept-data-agent.md)
|March 2026|**Fabric Maps in Real-Time Intelligence (Generally Available)**|[Fabric Maps (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/maps-in-microsoft-fabric-generally-available?ft=All) let you visualize real-time and historical location data in Microsoft Fabric with support for Ontology entities, scheduled tileset refreshes, WMS/WMTS raster services, Microsoft Planetary Computer Pro imagery, and data-driven styling. For more information, see [What is Fabric Maps?](../real-time-intelligence/map/about-fabric-maps.md)|
|March 2026|**Mirroring from SAP databases (Generally Available)**|You can continuously replicate your SAP data directly into Fabric's OneLake. Once in Fabric, you can take advantage of powerful capabilities for business intelligence, AI, data engineering, data science, and data sharing. For more information, see [Mirroring SAP](../mirroring/sap.md).|
|March 2026|**Preview-only steps for Dataflow Gen2 (Generally Available)**| Preview-only steps are transformation steps in Dataflow Gen2 that run only during the authoring phase for the data preview. They're excluded from run operations, ensuring they don't affect runtime behavior or production logic. For more information, see [preview-only step in Dataflow Gen2](../data-factory/dataflow-gen2-preview-only-step.md).|
|March 2026|**Schema support in Fabric data destinations (Generally Available)**|[Schema support in Fabric data destinations (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/fabric-march-2026-feature-summary/#post-34196-_Toc224559674) enables Dataflow Gen2 to write into specific schemas for Fabric SQL databases, Lakehouses, and Warehouses, so teams can organize tables by domain and improve collaboration in shared environments without creating separate destinations. For more information, see [Dataflow Gen2 data destinations and managed settings](../data-factory/dataflow-gen2-data-destinations-and-managed-settings.md).|
|March 2026|**AI-Powered Prompt Transform (Generally Available)**|[AI-Powered Prompt Transform (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/fabric-march-2026-feature-summary/#post-34196-_Toc224559675) integrates generative AI into low-code data transformation in Dataflow Gen2, so authors can enrich and transform data by using natural language prompts without building or managing machine learning models, with operations accounted towards an explicit AI meter. For more information, see [Fabric AI Prompt in Dataflow Gen2](../data-factory/dataflow-gen2-ai-functions.md).|
|March 2026|**IBM Netezza ODBC Driver connector for Power Query (Generally Available)**|The [IBM Netezza ODBC Driver (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/fabric-march-2026-feature-summary/#post-34196-_Toc224559685) provides reliable IBM Netezza connectivity by shifting from the embedded Simba driver to customer-provided IBM Netezza ODBC drivers, ensuring long-term support and a future-ready experience with existing connector reuse. For more information, see [IBM Netezza database connector](/power-query/connectors/ibm-netezza-database).|
|March 2026|**Google BigQuery connector for Power Query (Generally Available)**|The [Google BigQuery connector (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/fabric-march-2026-feature-summary/#post-34196-_Toc224559686) provides improved reliability and alignment with security standards. It's designed for durability, compliance, and future enhancements. For more information, see [Google BigQuery connector](/power-query/connectors/google-bigquery).|
|March 2026|**PowerShell model for gateways (Generally Available)**|[PowerShell model for gateways (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/fabric-march-2026-feature-summary/#post-34196-_Toc224559695) delivers fully supported, production-ready automation for gateway lifecycle, update, restore, and configuration management with new commands for version discovery and upgrade control. It makes large-scale script-driven gateway operations easier and more robust. For more information, see [PowerShell support for on-premises data gateways](/data-integration/gateway/service-gateway-powershell-support).|
|March 2026|**Certificate and proxy support for VNet data gateway (Generally Available)**|[Certificate and proxy support for VNet data gateway (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/certificate-and-proxy-support-for-vnet-data-gateway-generally-available?ft=All) enables certificate-based authentication and proxy routing for VNet data gateways in enterprise environments where direct outbound internet access is restricted. For more information, see [Manage virtual network (VNet) data gateways](/data-integration/vnet/manage-data-gateways).|
|March 2026|**AutoML low code user experience in Fabric (Generally Available)**|[AutoML, or Automated Machine Learning](../data-science/automated-machine-learning-fabric.md), is a process that automates the time-consuming and complex tasks of developing machine learning models. The new low code AutoML experience supports various tasks, including regression, forecasting, classification, and multi-class classification. To get started, see [Create models with Automated ML (preview)](../data-science/how-to-use-automated-machine-learning-fabric.md).|
|March 2026|**AI functions helpers for multimodal workflows (Preview)**|New AI functions helpers simplify multimodal file processing: `aifunc.load` ingests files from a folder into a table with optional prompt and schema, `aifunc.list_file_paths` enumerates file URLs for use in AI functions, and `ai.infer_schema` infers extraction schemas compatible with `ai.extract`. For more information, see [Transform and enrich data with AI functions](../data-science/ai-functions/overview.md).|
|March 2026|**Fabric notebook public APIs (Generally Available)**|[Fabric notebook public APIs (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/fabric-notebook-public-apis-generally-available?ft=All) enable you to programmatically manage and execute notebooks with full CRUD support via the Items REST API and on-demand execution via the Job Scheduler API, including support for returning exit values from runs for conditional orchestration and signaling outcomes, with monitoring and cancellation of job instances, and service principal authentication. For more information, see [Items - REST API (Core)](/rest/api/fabric/core/items) and [Job Scheduler - REST API (Core)](/rest/api/fabric/core/job-scheduler).|
|March 2026|**Outbound Access Protection (OAP) for Warehouse (Generally Available)**|[Outbound Access Protection (OAP) support for Warehouse (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/fabric-march-2026-feature-summary/#post-34196-_Toc224559641) provides stronger data exfiltration protection for enterprise environments, with connector rules that allow you to control external sources including specific Azure Data Lake Storage Gen2 accounts, other Fabric workspaces, and approved external connectors. For more information, see [Workspace outbound access protection for data warehouse workloads](../security/workspace-outbound-access-protection-data-warehouse.md).|
|March 2026|**Workspace-level workload assignment and centralized admin**|Workspace admins can now add workloads directly to one or more workspaces. In the [Workloads Hub](https://app.fabric.microsoft.com/workloadhub), admins can [add workloads directly to a workspace](../workload-development-kit/more-workloads-add.md). The Fabric Admin Portal also now includes a dedicated **Manage Workloads** tab, a single pane of glass for workload governance across your organization.|
|March 2026|**Fabric Extensibility Toolkit (Generally Available)**|The [Extensibility Toolkit](../extensibility-toolkit/key-concepts.md) creates the opportunity for partners and customers to build, validate, and publish custom Fabric workloads to production with full Microsoft support. The [Fabric Community Repository](https://aka.ms/fabric-extensibility-toolkit-samples) contains a wide variety of item types built with the Extensibility toolkit that you can add to your tenant. [CI/CD, Remote Lifecycle Notifications, and Fabric Scheduler (Preview)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/fabric-extensibility-toolkit-ci-cd-remote-lifecycle-notifications-and-fabric-scheduler-preview?ft=All) have also recently been added to the Extensibility Toolkit. For more information, see [Extensibility Toolkit documentation](https://aka.ms/fabric-extensibility-toolkit-docs).|
|March 2026|**Workspace tags (Generally Available)**|[Workspace tags](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/find-and-manage-workspaces-faster-with-workspace-tags-generally-available?ft=All) add shared context at the workspace level, so teams can organize workspaces by team, project, or cost center, filter workspaces by tags in the workspaces list and OneLake Catalog Explorer, and manage tags at scale by using APIs. For more information, see [Fabric tags overview](../governance/tags-overview.md) and [Define tags](../governance/tags-define.md).|
|March 2026|**Govern in OneLake Catalog for Fabric admins (Generally Available)**|[OneLake catalog governance for Fabric admins](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/onelake-catalog-govern-for-fabric-admins) provides admin insights, recommended actions, and reports in the Govern tab to improve governance across capacities, domains, and items. For more information, see [OneLake catalog](../governance/onelake-catalog-overview.md) and [Governance in OneLake catalog](../governance/onelake-catalog-govern.md).|
|March 2026|**On-premises data gateway auto-update (admin triggered) (Generally Available)**|[On-premises data gateway auto-update (admin triggered)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/on-premises-data-gateway-auto-update-admin-triggered-generally-available?ft=All) allows administrators to trigger gateway updates on demand instead of relying on automatic installation timing. This capability enables control over update timing to align with maintenance windows and programmatic updates via PowerShell. For more information, see [Update an on-premises data gateway](/data-integration/gateway/service-gateway-update).|
|March 2026|**Warehouse SQL Audit Logs (Generally Available)**|[SQL Audit Logs](../data-warehouse/sql-audit-logs.md) in Fabric Data Warehouse and SQL analytics endpoints provide a comprehensive and immutable record of all database activities. They capture critical details such as the event timestamp, the user or process that triggered the action, and the executed T-SQL statements. To get started, see [How to configure SQL audit logs](../data-warehouse/configure-sql-audit-logs.md).|
|March 2026|**OneLake as a source for COPY INTO and OPENROWSET (Generally Available)**|The `COPY INTO` and `OPENROWSET` T-SQL statements can read directly from OneLake paths in Fabric Data Warehouse, enabling SQL-based data ingestion and ad hoc querying from Lakehouse folders without external storage or complex setup. For more information, see [Ingest data into the Warehouse](../data-warehouse/ingest-data.md).|
|March 2026|**Oracle database mirroring in Microsoft Fabric (Generally Available)**|[Oracle database mirroring in Microsoft Fabric](../mirroring/oracle.md) is now generally available, including support updates such as Oracle Autonomous Database. For more information, see [Mirroring Oracle Databases](../mirroring/oracle.md), [Tutorial: Set up Oracle database mirroring](../mirroring/oracle-tutorial.md), and [Oracle mirroring limitations](../mirroring/oracle-limitations.md).|
|March 2026|**SQL database Dynamic Data Masking (DDM) (GA)**|[Dynamic data masking](/sql/relational-databases/security/dynamic-data-masking?view=fabric-sqldb&preserve-view=true) limits sensitive data exposure by masking it to nonprivileged users. It can greatly simplify the design and coding of security in your application.|
|March 2026|**Fabric SQL database customer-managed keys (GA)**|[Customer-managed keys in SQL database](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/customer-managed-keys-cmk-in-fabric-sql-database-generally-available?ft=All) let you use your own Azure Key Vault keys for workspace SQL database encryption with automatic TDE and key rotation control. For more information, see [Data encryption in SQL database](../database/sql/encryption.md) and [Customer-managed keys for Fabric workspaces](../security/workspace-customer-managed-keys.md).|
|March 2026 | **Microsoft Entra service principal support for Amazon S3 Shortcuts**|You can [use Microsoft Entra service principals to access Amazon S3 via OneLake Shortcuts](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/24780?ft=All), eliminating the need for long-term AWS access keys. This integration uses OpenID Connect (OIDC) for short-lived, standards-based tokens, simplifies cross-cloud identity management, and enables full auditability via AWS CloudTrail. To get started, see [AWS S3 shortcuts using service principal authentication](../onelake/amazon-storage-shortcut-entra-integration.md).|
|February 2026|**Modern evaluator for Dataflow Gen2 (Generally Available)**| The Modern Query Evaluation Engine (Modern Evaluator) for Dataflow Gen2 provides a new query execution engine running on .NET core version 8, which can significantly improve the performance of dataflow runs in some scenarios. For more information, see [the Modern evaluator for Dataflow Gen2](../data-factory/dataflow-gen2-modern-evaluator.md).|
|February 2026|**CI/CD for API for GraphQL (Generally Available)**|With the CI/CD for API for GraphQL, teams can manage GraphQL items in Git, collaborate with familiar pull-request workflows, and promote changes across environments using CI/CD. For more information, see [Source control and deployment pipelines in API for GraphQL](../data-engineering/graphql-source-control-and-deployment.md).|
|February 2026|**Snowflake Key-Pair Authentication (Generally Available)**|[Snowflake Key-Pair authentication](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/snowflake-key-pair-authentication-generally-available?ft=All) is now generally available, providing password-less RSA/ECDSA cryptographic key authentication for Snowflake connections across Power BI semantic models, Dataflow Gen2, Data pipelines, Copy jobs, and Mirroring. For more information, see [Snowflake connector Key-Pair authentication](../data-factory/connector-snowflake.md#key-pair-authentication).|
|February 2026|**Semantic Link (Generally Available)**|[Semantic Link](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/supercharge-ai-bi-and-data-engineering-with-semantic-link-generally-available?ft=All) is now generally available, connecting AI, BI, and data engineering through a shared semantic layer that enables data scientists, BI engineers, and data engineers to use semantic models directly in notebooks, automate Power BI tasks, and streamline Spark and SQL operations. For more information, see [Spark Runtime 2.0](../data-engineering/runtime-2-0.md) and [Semantic Link overview](../data-science/semantic-link-overview.md).|
|February 2026|**Default domain labels in Fabric (Generally Available)**|[Default domain sensitivity labels](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/governance-on-autopilot-the-power-of-default-domain-labels-in-fabric-generally-available?ft=All) are now generally available. They automatically apply sensitivity labels to new items created within a domain so that data is classified correctly from creation without manual steps. For more information, see [Domain-level default sensitivity labels](../governance/domain-default-sensitivity-label.md).|
|February 2026|**Microsoft OneLake and Snowflake interoperability (Generally Available)**|[OneLake and Snowflake interoperability](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/microsoft-onelake-and-snowflake-interoperability-is-now-generally-available?ft=All) enables bidirectional reads of Iceberg data, native storage of Snowflake-managed Iceberg tables in OneLake, automatic Fabric data conversion to Iceberg format for Snowflake access, and new UI experiences including a Snowflake item in OneLake. For more information, see [Snowflake with Iceberg tables in OneLake](../onelake/onelake-iceberg-snowflake.md) and [OneLake developer guidance](../onelake/onelake-access-api.md).|
|February 2026|**Data Series Colors (Generally Available)**|[Data Series Colors in Real-Time Dashboards](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/32713?ft=All) gives authors direct control over color assignments for each data series across pie, time, line, area, bar, column, anomaly, and scatter charts, enabling consistent visual storytelling and meaningful color-coded insights. For more information, see [Customize Real-Time Dashboard visuals](../real-time-intelligence/dashboard-visuals-customize.md).|
|February 2026|**Mirroring Azure Databricks catalogs from Azure Databricks workspaces behind private endpoints (Generally Available)**|[Mirroring Azure Databricks catalogs](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/mirroring-azure-databricks-catalogs-from-azure-databricks-workspaces-behind-private-endpoints-generally-available?ft=All) from Azure Databricks workspaces behind private endpoints uses the Virtual Network data gateway to establish secure private connectivity. This capability enables Unity Catalog metadata and data to mirror into Fabric while maintaining network isolation. For more information, see [Mirroring Azure Databricks Unity Catalog](../mirroring/azure-databricks.md) and [Mirroring from workspaces accessible only through private endpoints](../mirroring/azure-databricks-private-endpoint.md).|
|February 2026|**OneLake Table APIs (Generally Available)**|[OneLake Table APIs](../onelake/table-apis/table-apis-overview.md) are generally available, enabling programmatic management of tables in OneLake using Apache Iceberg REST Catalog and Delta Lake APIs. For more information, see [OneLake Table APIs](../onelake/table-apis/table-apis-overview.md).|
|January 2026|**Fabric Identities (Generally Available)**|[Fabric Identities tenant limit control](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/take-control-of-fabric-identities-limit-for-your-tenant-generally-available?ft=All) increases the default limit from 1,000 to 10,000 identities and enables tenant admins to set custom limits for Fabric identities (workspace identities) via admin portal or REST API. For more information, see [Workspace identity](../security/workspace-identity.md) and [Tenant settings index](../admin/tenant-settings-index.md).|
|January 2026|**MERGE support**|The [MERGE T-SQL syntax](/sql/t-sql/statements/merge-transact-sql?view=fabric&preserve-view=true) is now generally available for Fabric Data Warehouse. This DML statement provides a sleek and uniform approach for executing transformations based on conditions between a Source table and Target table. Perform INSERTs, UPDATEs, and DELETEs all in a single command with MERGE.|
| March 2026 | **Notebook Public APIs (Generally Available)** | Developers can manage notebooks with full CRUD lifecycle via the [Items REST API](/rest/api/fabric/notebook/items) and execute notebooks on demand via the [Job Scheduler API](/rest/api/fabric/core/job-scheduler), with support for parameters, environment and Lakehouse selection, run monitoring, and canceling jobs. Runs return an exit value for conditional orchestration and downstream signaling. Service principal authentication is supported for both management (Items REST API) and execution (Job Scheduler) for secure unattended automation and CI/CD. For more information, see [Manage and execute notebooks in Fabric with APIs](../data-engineering/notebook-public-api.md). |
| December 2025 | **DATE_BUCKET() function in Fabric Data Warehouse (Generally Available)** | The [DATE_BUCKET() function in Fabric Data Warehouse](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/date_bucket-function-in-fabric-data-warehouse) enables custom time-based aggregations (for example, 2 months or 3 weeks) with `DATE_BUCKET(unit, length, datetime)`. For more information, see [DATE_BUCKET (T-SQL)](/sql/t-sql/functions/date-bucket-transact-sql?view=fabric&preserve-view=true). |
| December 2025 | **Fabric Data Warehouse incremental statistics refresh** | Incremental statistics refresh is a performance optimization to automatic statistic updates. It opportunistically reduces the duration of automatic statistic updates by only sampling newly added rows (instead of the entire column), speeding up user queries that must update statistics before running. For more information, see [Fabric Data Warehouse Statistics](../data-warehouse/statistics.md). |
| December 2025 | **Fabric Data Warehouse proactive statistics refresh** | With this feature enabled, column statistics that are automatically created during SELECT queries are now eligible to be proactively refreshed after data changes. This reduces the chances of a user query having to wait for statistic updates before being able to run, reducing user query time. For more information, see [Fabric Data Warehouse Statistics](../data-warehouse/statistics.md). |
|December 2025|**Lakehouse schemas (Generally Available)**|[Lakehouse schemas, now generally available](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/lakehouse-schemas-generally-available?ft=All) allow you to group your tables together for better data discovery, access control, and more. For more information, see [Lakehouse schemas](../data-engineering/lakehouse-schemas.md).|

The new monitoring experience includes a new Recent run panel and a dedicated T-SQL panel to list the query history. To learn more, see [T-SQL support in Microsoft Fabric notebooks](../data-engineering/author-tsql-notebook.md).|
|June 2025|**Azure database for PostgreSQL connector 2.0**|The [Azure database for PostgreSQL connector](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/on-premises-data-gateway-june-2025-release?ft=All) version 2.0 is now generally available. This new version is enhanced to support TLS 1.3, the upsert table action, as well as the script activity in data pipeline.|
|June 2025|**Incremental Copy GA, Lakehouse Upserts, and New Connectors**|Incremental copy is now generally available, you can now choose to merge data directly into more destination stores, and more connectors with Copy job are now available. For more information, see [Simplifying Data Ingestion with Copy job](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/simplifying-data-ingestion-with-copy-job-incremental-copy-ga-lakehouse-upserts-and-new-connectors?ft=All).|
|June 2025 |**Capacity pools**|[Capacity administrators can now create custom pools](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/introducing-capacity-pools-for-data-engineering-and-data-science-in-microsoft-fabric?ft=All) based on their workload requirements, providing granular control over compute resources. [Custom pools for Data Engineering and Data Science](../data-engineering/capacity-settings-management.md#capacity-pools-for-data-engineering-and-data-science-in-microsoft-fabric) can be set as Spark Pool options within Workspace Spark Settings and environment items. |
|June 2025|**Boost performance effortlessly with Automated Table Statistics in Fabric Spark**|[Automated Table Statistics](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/boost-performance-effortlessly-with-automated-table-statistics-in-microsoft-fabric?ft=All) are now generally available, automatically optimizing query performance by maintaining up-to-date statistics in Fabric Spark. For more information, see [Configure and manage Automated Table Statistics in Fabric Spark](../data-engineering/automated-table-statistics.md).|
|May 2025|**Azure Data Factory item in Microsoft Fabric**|[Azure Data Factory is now generally available in Microsoft Fabric](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/23604?ft=All) allows you to seamlessly [connect your existing Azure Data Factory (ADF) pipelines to Fabric workspaces](../data-factory/tutorial-bring-azure-data-factory-to-fabric.md), eliminating the need to manually rebuild or migrate them. [CI/CD and REST APIs support is also for the Azure Data Factory items](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/data-operations-in-fabric-data-factory?ft=All) in Microsoft Fabric.|
|May 2025|**Fabric CLI**|The Fabric CLI (`fab`) is a fast, file-system-inspired command-line interface for Microsoft Fabric. Explore, automate, and script your Fabric environment—right from your terminal. Get started at [https://aka.ms/FabCLI](https://aka.ms/FabCLI).|
|May 2025|**Eventhouse Query Acceleration for OneLake Shortcuts**|[Query Acceleration for OneLake Shortcuts in Eventhouse](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/eventhouse-accelerated-onelake-table-shortcuts-generally-available?ft=All) speeds up ad hoc queries over data in OneLake. OneLake shortcuts are references from an Eventhouse that point to internal Fabric or external sources. Previously, queries run over OneLake shortcuts were less performant than on data that is ingested directly to Eventhouses due to various factors. For more information, see [Query acceleration for OneLake shortcuts - overview](../real-time-intelligence/query-acceleration-overview.md).|
|May 2025|**Task flows in Microsoft Fabric**|With [Task flows](../fundamentals/task-flow-overview.md), now generally available, you no longer need to use a whiteboard to sketch out the different parts of the project and their interrelationships. Instead, you can use a task flow to build and bring this key information into the project itself. For more information, see [Task flows in Microsoft Fabric (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/announcing-the-general-availability-ga-of-task-flows-in-microsoft-fabric?ft=All).|
|May 2025|**Microsoft Fabric Spark Native Execution Engine now generally available**|[The Microsoft Fabric Spark Native Execution Engine is now generally available](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/microsoft-fabric-spark-native-execution-engine-now-generally-available?ft=All) as part of Fabric Runtime 1.3 and provides improved performance and efficiency for Spark workloads in Microsoft Fabric. For more information, see [Native execution engine for Fabric Spark](../data-engineering/native-execution-engine-overview.md).|
|May 2025|**Dataflow Gen2 CI/CD support**|[CI/CD and Git integration](../data-factory/dataflow-gen2-cicd-and-git-integration.md) are now supported for Dataflow Gen2 as a generally available feature. For more information, see [Dataflow Gen2 CI/CD support](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/dataflow-gen2-ci-cd-git-integration-and-public-apis?ft=All).|
|May 2025|**OneLake shortcut cache and on-premises gateway support now generally available**|[Shortcut cache and on-premises gateway support is now generally available](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/shortcut-cache-and-on-prem-gateway-support-now-generally-available?ft=All). Use OneLake shortcut cache to quickly and easily source data from external cloud providers. The on-premises gateway allows you to securely connect to your data through multiple network restricted scenarios. For more information, see [Create shortcuts to on-premises data](../onelake/create-on-premises-shortcut.md).|
|May 2025|**Open mirroring**|[Open mirroring](../mirroring/open-mirroring.md) enables any application to write change data directly into a mirrored database in Fabric, based on the open mirroring public APIs and approach. [Open mirroring](https://aka.ms/openmirroringga), now generally available, is designed to be extensible, customizable, and open. It's a powerful feature that extends mirroring in Fabric based on open Delta Lake table format. To get started, see [Tutorial: Configure Microsoft Fabric open mirrored databases](../mirroring/open-mirroring-tutorial.md).|
|May 2025|**JSON Aggregate support**|Fabric warehouses now support JSON aggregate functions as generally available features. For more information, see [JSON_ARRAYAGG](/sql/t-sql/functions/json-arrayagg-transact-sql?view=fabric&preserve-view=true) and [JSON_OBJECTAGG](/sql/t-sql/functions/json-objectagg-transact-sql?view=fabric&preserve-view=true).|
|May 2025|**Semantic model refresh activity**|Use the [Semantic model refresh activity to refresh a Power BI Dataset](../data-factory/semantic-model-refresh-activity.md), the most effective way to refresh your Fabric semantic models. For more information, see [Semantic Model Refresh Activity (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/fabric-may-2025-feature-summary?ft=All#post-23234-_Toc198140725).|
|April 2025|**Fabric Spark connector for Fabric Data Warehouse in Spark runtime**|The [Spark connector for Data Warehouse](../data-engineering/spark-data-warehouse-connector.md), now generally available, enables a Spark developer or a data scientist to access and work on data from a warehouse or SQL analytics endpoint of the lakehouse (either from within the same workspace or from across workspaces) with a simplified Spark API. |
|April 2025|**Session-scoped distributed #temp tables**|[Distributed session-scoped temporary tables](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/announcing-the-general-availability-of-session-scoped-distributed-temp-tables-in-fabric-data-warehouse?ft=All) in Fabric Data Warehouse and Fabric Lakehouse SQL analytics endpoints are now generally available. Now, `#temp` tables are supported as session scoped or local temp tables. For more information, see [Tables in Fabric Data Warehouse](../data-warehouse/tables.md#temp-tables-in-fabric-data-warehouse).|
|April 2025|**BULK INSERT support**|The T-SQL [BULK INSERT statement](/sql/t-sql/statements/bulk-insert-transact-sql?view=fabric&preserve-view=true) in Fabric Data Warehouse is now generally available. For more information, see [BULK INSERT statement is generally available](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/bulk-insert-statement-is-generally-available?ft=All).| 
|April 2025|**Multi-tenant organization (MTO)**|Support for multitenant organizations in Fabric is now generally available (GA). [Microsoft Entra ID users of type external member](/fabric/enterprise/powerbi/service-admin-entra-b2b) are supported across the Fabric platform.|
|April 2025|**Tags**| [Tags help admins categorize and organize data](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/fabric-march-2025-feature-summary?ft=All#post-20656-_Toc193974191), enhancing the searchability of your data and boosting success rates and efficiency for end users. [Tags in Microsoft Fabric](../governance/tags-overview.md) are now generally available.|
|April 2025|**OneLake SAS**|Support for short-lived, user-delegated [OneLake SAS](../onelake/onelake-shared-access-signature-overview.md) is now generally available. This functionality allows applications to request a User Delegation Key backed by Microsoft Entra ID, and then use this key to construct a OneLake SAS token. This token can be handed off to provide delegated access to another tool, node, or user, ensuring secure and controlled access.|
|April 2025|**Data pipeline capabilities in Copilot for Data Factory**|[Data pipeline capabilities in Copilot for Data Factory](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/ai-powered-development-with-data-factory-microsoft-fabric?ft=All) are now generally available. These features function as an AI expert to help users build, troubleshoot, and maintain data pipelines.|
|April 2025|**CI/CD for Fabric Data Pipelines**|[Git Integration and integration with built-in Deployment Pipelines to Data Factory data pipelines](../data-factory/cicd-pipelines.md) is now generally available. For more information, see [CI/CD for Data pipelines](../data-factory/cicd-pipelines.md) and [REST API capabilities for Data pipelines](../data-factory/pipeline-rest-api-capabilities.md).|
|April 2025|**Data Factory Apache Airflow jobs**|[Apache Airflow job in Data Factory](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/running-apache-airflow-jobs-seamlessly-in-microsoft-fabric?ft=All), powered by Apache Airflow, are now generally available. An Apache Airflow Job in Microsoft Fabric offers seamless authoring, scheduling, and monitoring experience for Python-based data processes defined as Directed Acyclic Graphs (DAGs). For more information, see [Quickstart: Create an Apache Airflow Job](../data-factory/create-apache-airflow-jobs.md).|
|April 2025|**High concurrency mode for Notebooks in Pipelines**|[High concurrency mode for notebooks in pipelines](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/announcing-general-availability-of-high-concurrency-mode-for-notebooks-in-pipelines?ft=All), now generally available, enables users to share Spark sessions across multiple notebooks within a pipeline. With [high concurrency mode](../data-engineering/high-concurrency-overview.md), users can trigger pipeline jobs, and these jobs are automatically packed into existing high concurrency sessions. |
|April 2025|**OPENROWSET support**|The T-SQL [OPENROWSET(BULK) function](/sql/t-sql/functions/openrowset-bulk-transact-sql?view=fabric&preserve-view=true) is now generally available in Fabric warehouse. For more examples, see [Browse file content using OPENROWSET function](../data-warehouse/browse-file-content-with-openrowset.md). For more information, see [OPENROWSET function in Fabric Data Warehouse now generally available](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/the-openrowset-function-is-generally-available-in-fabric-data-warehouse).|
|March 2025|**Terraform provider GA**|The Terraform Provider for Microsoft Fabric is now generally available, enabling seamless infrastructure management and automation. For more information, use cases, and benefits, see [Terraform Provider for Microsoft Fabric (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/terraform-provider-for-microsoft-fabric-now-generally-available?ft=All).|
|February 2025|**REST APIs for Fabric Data Factory pipelines**|The [Fabric data pipeline public REST API](../data-factory/pipeline-rest-api-capabilities.md) enables you to extend the built-in capability in Fabric to create, read, update, delete, and list pipelines.|
|February 2025|**Copy job**|The [*Copy job* in Data Factory](../data-factory/what-is-copy-job.md) has advantages over the Copy activity. For more information, see [What is the Copy Job in Microsoft Fabric](../data-factory/what-is-copy-job.md). For a tutorial, see [Learn how to create a Copy job in Data Factory for Microsoft Fabric](../data-factory/create-copy-job.md).|
|February 2025|**Nested Common Table Expressions (CTEs) (GA)**|Fabric Data Warehouse and SQL analytics endpoint both support [*standard*, *sequential*, and *nested* CTEs as generally available features](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/fabric-february-2025-feature-summary?ft=All#post-19077-_Toc346130597) now. For more information, see [nested common table expressions (CTE) in Fabric data warehousing (Transact-SQL)](/sql/t-sql/queries/nested-common-table-expression?view=fabric&preserve-view=true). |
|January 2025|**Real-time intelligence ALM and REST API GA**|Application Lifecycle Management (ALM) and Fabric REST APIs are now generally available for all RTI items: Eventstream, Eventhouse, KQL Database, Realtime dashboard, Query set and Data Activator. ALM includes both [deployment pipelines](../cicd/deployment-pipelines/intro-to-deployment-pipelines.md) and [Git integration](../cicd/deployment-pipelines/intro-to-deployment-pipelines.md). REST APIs allow you to programmatically create / read / update / delete items.|
|January 2025|**Warehouse restore points and restore in place**|You can now [create restore points and perform an in-place restore of a warehouse](../data-warehouse/restore-in-place.md) to a past point in time. [Restore in-place is an essential part of data warehouse recovery](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/the-art-of-data-warehouse-recovery-within-microsoft-fabric), which allows to restore the data warehouse to a prior known reliable state by replacing or over-writing the existing data warehouse from which the restore point was created. |

## Microsoft Fabric platform features

Archived news and feature announcements about the Microsoft Fabric platform experience.

|**Month** | **Feature** | **Learn more** |
|:-- |:-- | :-- |
|April 2026|**Tabbed multitasking and object explorer (Generally Available)**|[Tabbed multitasking and object explorer (Generally Available)](https://community.fabric.microsoft.com/t5/Fabric-Updates-Blog/Fabric-April-2026-Feature-Summary/ba-p/5176490) deliver fully supported tabs for working across multiple Fabric items in parallel, plus an object explorer that browses items across open workspaces. The GA release adds right-click tab management, open-in-new-window, a resizable explorer pane, support for opening monitoring jobs as tabs, and accessibility improvements. For more information, see [Multitask with tabs and object explorer](./fabric-home.md#multitask-with-tabs-and-object-explorer).|
|April 2026|**Create AI Auto-Description for Semantic Models (Preview)**|[Auto-Description for Semantic Models (Preview)](https://community.fabric.microsoft.com/t5/Fabric-Updates-Blog/Fabric-April-2026-Feature-Summary/ba-p/5176490) uses Copilot to generate clear descriptions for semantic models from the model's metadata and structure, which model owners and contributors can review, edit, and regenerate directly from the semantic model details page in the OneLake catalog. For more information, see [OneLake catalog overview](../governance/onelake-catalog-overview.md).|
|April 2026|**Manage failure notifications from the monitoring hub in Fabric (Preview)**|The [Schedule failures page in the Fabric monitoring hub (Preview)](https://community.fabric.microsoft.com/t5/Fabric-Updates-Blog/Manage-failure-notifications-from-the-monitoring-hub-in-Fabric/ba-p/5160381) lists every scheduled item with failure notifications configured and lets you add, edit, or remove recipients for any item from one place, without opening each item individually. For more information, see [Schedule failures (preview)](../admin/monitoring-hub.md#schedule-failures-preview) and [Receive notifications for failed scheduled jobs](job-scheduler.md#receive-notifications-for-failed-scheduled-jobs).|
|April 2026|**Resource instance rules for OneLake (Preview)**|[Resource instance rules for OneLake (Preview)](https://community.fabric.microsoft.com/t5/Fabric-Updates-Blog/Resource-instance-rules-for-OneLake-in-Microsoft-Fabric-Preview/ba-p/5171998) let workspace admins allow inbound access to OneLake from explicitly trusted Azure resource instances by identity, complementing Private Link and IP firewall rules for service-to-service scenarios without requiring IP allow lists or private networking. For more information, see [Manage inbound access to OneLake with Resource Instance Rules](../onelake/onelake-manage-inbound-access-trusted-resources.md).|
|April 2026|**Outbound access protection for Data Factory (Generally Available)**|[Workspace outbound access protection (OAP) for Data Factory (Generally Available)](https://community.fabric.microsoft.com/t5/Fabric-Updates-Blog/Outbound-access-protection-for-Data-Factory-Generally-Available/ba-p/5172006) extends workspace-level outbound controls to Pipelines, Copy Job, Dataflows, and Mirrored Databases (including Mirrored SQL Database and Mirrored Snowflake), so Data Factory items in a protected workspace only connect to admin-allowed endpoints. Data Agent and Eventstreams gain OAP support in preview. For more information, see [Workspace outbound access protection overview](../security/workspace-outbound-access-protection-overview.md) and [Workspace outbound access protection for Data Factory](../security/workspace-outbound-access-protection-data-factory.md).|
|April 2026|**Fabric Local MCP (Generally Available)** and **Fabric Remote MCP (Preview)**|[Agentic Fabric: How MCP is turning your data platform into an AI-native operating system](https://community.fabric.microsoft.com/t5/Fabric-Updates-Blog/Agentic-Fabric-How-MCP-is-turning-your-data-platform-into-an-AI/ba-p/5172009) introduces two Model Context Protocol entry points to Fabric: Local MCP, an open-source on-machine server that grounds AI assistants in Fabric APIs, OneLake file operations, and Fabric item operations, and Remote MCP, a cloud-hosted server that lets agents perform authenticated workspace, item, search, permission, and connection operations through Microsoft Entra ID with full audit logging. The Fabric Remote MCP server is also available as a preview feature. For more information, see [Get started with Fabric Pro-Dev MCP Server](/rest/api/fabric/articles/mcp-servers/pro-dev-local/get-started-local) and [Get started with Fabric Core MCP Server](/rest/api/fabric/articles/mcp-servers/core-remote/get-started-core).|
|April 2026|**Shortcut transformations (Generally Available)**|[Shortcut transformations](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/shortcut-transformations-and-turn-files-into-delta-tables-without-pipelines-generally-available?ft=All) automatically turn structured files into Delta tables as you bring data into or move it within OneLake, keeping data always in sync without the need for pipelines. For more information, see [Shortcuts file transformations](../onelake/shortcuts/transformations.md).|
|April 2026|**Workspace customer-managed keys for BYOK (Preview)**|[Workspace customer-managed keys (CMK) for BYOK (Preview)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/workspace-customer-managed-keys-for-byok-in-microsoft-fabric-preview?ft=All) enables workspace-level CMK in BYOK-enabled Fabric capacities, so you can use the same or separate Azure Key Vault keys for Power BI semantic models and other Fabric items without provisioning dedicated capacities. For more information, see [Customer-managed keys for Fabric workspaces](../security/workspace-customer-managed-keys.md).|
|April 2026|**Associate an identity for items (Preview)**|[Associated identities for items (Preview)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/associated-identities-for-items-preview?ft=All) let you associate a user, service principal, or managed identity with Fabric Lakehouses and Eventstreams via REST API, removing the dependency on the item owner. For more information, see [Manage identities associated with Fabric items](/rest/api/fabric/articles/item-management/associate-item-identity).|
|March 2026|**Sensitivity labels in Fabric public APIs (Generally Available)**|[Sensitivity labels in Fabric public APIs (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/sensitivity-labels-in-fabric-for-public-apis-generally-available?ft=All) expose sensitivity label metadata through List Items, Get Item, and Update Item API responses, enabling programmatic classification monitoring, AI agent guardrails, and compliance automation. For more information, see [Sensitivity Labels in Fabric and Power BI](../governance/protected-sensitivity-labels.md).|
|March 2026|**Scheduled job failure notifications (Generally Available)**|[Scheduled job failure notifications (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/get-notified-when-scheduled-jobs-fail-in-fabric-generally-available?ft=All) send email alerts when scheduled runs of Pipelines, Notebooks, Dataflows Gen2, and other Fabric items fail, with error details and a link to the failed run in the Monitoring Hub. For more information, see [Job Scheduler documentation](https://aka.ms/ScheduledJobNotifications).|
|March 2026|**Capacity overage (Preview)**|[Capacity overage (Preview)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/introducing-capacity-overage-preview-flexibility-when-you-need-it-most?ft=All) is an opt-in capability that automatically bills for excess capacity usage during compute spikes instead of throttling, with admin-configurable limits per 24-hour window at 3x pay-as-you-go rates. For more information, see [Capacity overage in Microsoft Fabric](../enterprise/capacity-overage-overview.md).|
|March 2026|**Workspace IP firewall rules (Generally Available)** | [Workspace IP firewall rules](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/workspace-level-ip-firewall-rules-in-microsoft-fabric-generally-available?ft=All) let workspace admins define an allow list of public IP addresses or IP ranges that can access a Fabric workspace, helping limit inbound access to approved network locations. For more information, see [Protect workspaces by using IP firewall rules](../security/security-workspace-level-firewall-overview.md).|
|March 2026|**Git developer experiences (Preview)**|[New Git developer experiences (Preview)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/introducing-new-git-developer-experiences-in-microsoft-fabric-preview?ft=All) add [Branched Workspaces](../cicd/git-integration/branched-workspace.md) for formal source-to-feature workspace relationships, [Selective Branching](https://aka.ms/AAz2i48) to branch out with only the items you need, and the ability to [Compare Code Changes](https://aka.ms/AAzydxy) for rich diff review before committing or syncing.|

The capability is also included as a built-in tool in the Fabric Core MCP server for AI agents. The [Fabric CLI `fab find` command](https://community.fabric.microsoft.com/t5/Fabric-Updates-Blog/Discover-items-across-workspaces-with-the-OneLake-Catalog-Search/ba-p/5176768) extends the search to the terminal so you can locate items across workspaces, filter or exclude by item type, and pipe results through JMESPath. ## Data Factory in Microsoft Fabric

This section summarizes archived new features and capabilities of [Data Factory in Microsoft Fabric](../data-factory/data-factory-overview.md). Follow issues and feedback through the [Data Factory Community Forum](https://community.fabric.microsoft.com/t5/Data-Factory-preview-Community/ct-p/datafactory).

|**Month** | **Feature** | **Learn more** |
|:-- |:-- | :-- |
|April 2026|**On-premises data gateway April 2026 release**|The [April 2026 on-premises data gateway release (version 3000.314)](https://community.fabric.microsoft.com/t5/Fabric-Updates-Blog/On-premises-data-gateway-April-2026-release/ba-p/5171981) brings the gateway up to date with the April 2026 Power BI Desktop release and reinforces on-premises Data Gateway Auto-Update (Admin Triggered) as Generally Available, so gateway administrators can manually trigger gateway updates on demand to align with maintenance windows. For more information, see [Update an on-premises data gateway](/data-integration/gateway/service-gateway-update).|
|April 2026|**Outbound access protection for Data Factory (Generally Available)**|[Workspace outbound access protection (OAP) for Data Factory (Generally Available)](https://community.fabric.microsoft.com/t5/Fabric-Updates-Blog/Outbound-access-protection-for-Data-Factory-Generally-Available/ba-p/5172006) extends workspace-level outbound controls to Pipelines, Copy Job, Dataflows, and Mirrored Databases (including Mirrored SQL Database and Mirrored Snowflake), so Data Factory items in a protected workspace only connect to admin-allowed endpoints. Data Agent and Eventstreams gain OAP support in preview. For more information, see [Workspace outbound access protection overview](../security/workspace-outbound-access-protection-overview.md) and [Workspace outbound access protection for Data Factory](../security/workspace-outbound-access-protection-data-factory.md).|
|March 2026|**Apache Airflow jobs and pipelines updates**|Latest [updates to Apache Airflow jobs and pipelines](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/announcing-the-latest-innovations-in-fabric-data-factory-apache-airflow-jobs-and-pipelines?ft=All) add Copy job and dbt job operator support for Airflow DAGs, a context menu shortcut to run Fabric items, new Airflow job APIs for programmatic DAG management, and interval-based schedules (preview) for non-overlapping pipeline runs. For more information, see [Create Apache Airflow job in Data Factory](../data-factory/create-apache-airflow-jobs.md).|
|March 2026|**Copy job CDC enhancements: Oracle source, Warehouse sink, and SCD Type 2 (Preview)**|[Recent updates to CDC in Copy job (Preview)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/simplifying-data-movement-across-multiple-clouds-with-richer-cdc-in-copy-job-in-fabric-data-factory-oracle-source-fabric-data-warehouse-sink-and-scd-type-2-preview?ft=All) adds Oracle as a CDC source, Fabric Data Warehouse as a CDC destination, and SCD Type 2 with built-in soft delete for full change history tracking, all configured without code. For more information, see [Change data capture (CDC) in Copy job](../data-factory/cdc-copy-job.md).|
|March 2026|**Copy job auto-partitioning (Preview)**|[Copy job auto-partitioning (Preview)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/higher-performance-with-copy-job-in-fabric-data-factory-auto-partitioning-preview?ft=All) automatically analyzes source schemas and data characteristics to partition large tables during data movement, and disables V-Order by default when writing to Lakehouse tables for 2X faster performance with no manual tuning. For more information, see [What is Copy job in Data Factory?](../data-factory/what-is-copy-job.md).|
|March 2026|**Fabric Migration Assessment for Data Factory (Preview)**|The new [Fabric Migration Assessment for Data Factory (Preview)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/new-migration-experience-from-azure-data-factory-to-fabric-preview?ft=All) provides a built-in assessment and migration experience that evaluates ADF pipeline readiness, categorizes pipelines as Ready, Needs Review, Coming Soon, or Unsupported, mounts ADF to a Fabric workspace, and migrates supported pipelines with connection mapping. For more information, see [Migration planning for Azure Data Factory](../data-factory/migrate-planning-azure-data-factory.md).|
|March 2026|**Fabric variable libraries in Dataflow Gen2 with CI/CD (Generally available)**|[Fabric variable libraries](/fabric/cicd/variable-library/variable-library-overview) offer a centralized way to manage configuration values across Microsoft Fabric workloads. With [integration in Dataflow Gen2](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/dataflow-gen2-variable-library-integration-in-microsoft-fabric-generally-available?ft=All), you can reference these variables directly in your dataflow, enabling dynamic behavior across environments and simplifying CI/CD workflows. For more information, see [variable libraries in Dataflow Gen2](../data-factory/dataflow-gen2-variable-library-integration.md).|
|March 2026|**Data Factory in Fabric connection recency (Preview)**|[Connection recency (Preview)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/connection-recency-for-improved-audit-and-management-preview?ft=All) adds last-linked-to-items and last-credentials-used properties to connections, helping you identify stale or unused connections and make safer cleanup decisions. For more information, see [Data source management](../data-factory/data-source-management.md#connection-recency-preview).|
|March 2026|**Lakehouse utility suite (Preview)**|The [Lakehouse Utility Suite](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/modernizing-pipelines-new-activities-and-innovations-in-fabric-data-factory-pipelines?ft=All) now includes the [Lakehouse maintenance activity (Preview)](https://aka.ms/LakehouseMaintenanceDocs), to automate routine Lakehouse upkeep tasks, and the [Refresh SQL endpoint activity (Preview)](https://aka.ms/RSQLDocs), to refresh the Lakehouse SQL analytics endpoint on demand or on a schedule within Fabric pipelines. |
|March 2026|**Dataflow Gen2 capabilities at FabCon Atlanta 2026**|[New Dataflow Gen2 capabilities](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/a-wave-of-new-dataflow-gen2-capabilities-at-fabcon-atlanta-2026?ft=All) include ADLS Gen2 and Lakehouse Files destinations (GA), relative references for portable dataflows (GA), email alerts for failed refreshes, scheduled runs with parameters, [Save as Dataflow](../data-factory/migrate-to-dataflow-gen2-using-save-as.md#save-a-dataflow-gen1-as-a-new-dataflow-gen2-cicd), previews for Snowflake and Excel file destinations, diagnostics download, publish-time destination checks, and the Execute Query Streaming API. For more information, see [Dataflow Gen2 overview](../data-factory/dataflows-gen2-overview.md).|

For more information, see [Connector overview](../data-factory/connector-overview.md).|

|March 2026|**Audit columns in Copy job**|[Audit columns in Copy job](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/audit-columns-in-copy-job-in-fabric-data-factory-every-row-is-traceable-for-data-lineage-and-compliance?ft=All) automatically append metadata such as extraction time, source file path, workspace ID, job name, and run ID to every row written to a destination, providing row-level data lineage for compliance, debugging, and freshness tracking. For more information, see [What is Copy job in Data Factory?](../data-factory/what-is-copy-job.md).|

|March 2026|**On-premises data gateway auto-update (admin triggered) (Generally Available)**|[On-premises data gateway auto-update (admin triggered)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/on-premises-data-gateway-auto-update-admin-triggered-generally-available?ft=All) allows administrators to trigger gateway updates on demand instead of relying on automatic installation timing. This capability enables control over update timing to align with maintenance windows and programmatic updates via PowerShell. For more information, see [Update an on-premises data gateway](/data-integration/gateway/service-gateway-update).|

For more information, see [Execute Query API Reference](/rest/api/fabric/dataflow/query-execution/execute-query).|

This preview feature makes tuning Data Factory simpler, safer, and more effective without requiring deep manual expertise or trial-and-error adjustments. To enable, see [the adaptivePerformanceTuning property when using copy activity](../data-factory/copy-data-activity.md#configure-your-other-settings-under-settings-tab).|

## Fabric Data Engineering

This section summarizes archived new features and capabilities of data engineering, including [Data Factory in Microsoft Fabric](../data-factory/data-factory-overview.md).

|**Month** | **Feature** |  **Learn more**|
|:-- |:-- | :-- |
|April 2026|**Maven support in Fabric Environment (Preview)**|[Maven support in Fabric Environment (Preview)](https://community.fabric.microsoft.com/t5/Fabric-Updates-Blog/Fabric-April-2026-Feature-Summary/ba-p/5176490) lets Scala and Java developers add libraries from Maven repositories to a Fabric Environment by uploading and managing `pom.xml` files directly, so transitive dependencies are resolved without manually downloading and uploading JARs. For more information, see [Manage libraries in Fabric environments](../data-engineering/environment-manage-library.md).|
|April 2026|**Nested folders support in shortcut transformations (Generally Available)**|[Nested folders support in shortcut transformations (Generally Available)](https://community.fabric.microsoft.com/t5/Fabric-Updates-Blog/Nested-folders-support-in-shortcut-transformations-Generally/ba-p/5171995) extends the zero-ETL shortcut transformations model to multi-level folder hierarchies with recursive change detection, automatic partition pickup, directory structure preservation, and a single Delta table output per top-level folder. The Include subfolders option is enabled by default for new and existing transformations. For more information, see [Shortcuts file transformations](../onelake/shortcuts/transformations.md).|
|April 2026|**Microsoft ADO.NET Driver for Fabric Data Engineering (Preview)**|The [Microsoft ADO.NET Driver for Fabric Data Engineering (Preview)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/microsoft-ado-net-driver-for-microsoft-fabric-data-engineering-preview?ft=All) lets .NET applications connect to Spark SQL in Fabric using standard ADO.NET patterns (DbConnection, DbCommand, DbDataReader) with Microsoft Entra ID authentication, connection pooling, session reuse, and async prefetch via Livy APIs. For more information, see [Microsoft ADO.NET driver for Fabric Data Engineering](../data-engineering/spark-adonet-driver.md).|
|March 2026|**Resources Folder in Git**|[Resources Folder support in Git](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/fabric-notebooks-resources-folder-support-in-git?ft=All) lets you commit the built-in Resources folder alongside notebooks to Git, with exclusion rules and .gitignore support to keep repositories clean. For more information, see [Notebook source control and deployment](../data-engineering/notebook-source-control-deployment.md).|
|March 2026|**Lakehouse auto-binding in Git (Preview)**|[Lakehouse auto-binding in Git (Preview)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/fabric-notebooks-support-lakehouse-auto-binding-in-git-preview?ft=All) resolves lakehouse references automatically as notebooks move across Git-connected workspaces, making notebooks portable across development, test, and production environments. For more information, see [Notebook source control and deployment](../data-engineering/notebook-source-control-deployment.md).|
|March 2026|**Microsoft JDBC Driver (Generally Available)**|The [Microsoft JDBC driver for Fabric Data Engineering (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/microsoft-jdbc-driver-for-microsoft-fabric-data-engineering-generally-available?ft=All) enables Java applications and BI tools to connect to Spark SQL in Fabric with JDBC 4.2 compliance, enterprise authentication, connection pooling, and async prefetch. For more information, see [Microsoft JDBC driver for Fabric Data Engineering](../data-engineering/spark-jdbc-driver.md).|
|March 2026|**Materialized Lake Views (Generally Available)**|[Materialized Lake Views (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/materialized-lake-views-in-microsoft-fabric-generally-available?ft=All) replace hand-built ETL pipelines with declarative Spark SQL or PySpark statements, adding multi-schedule support, broader incremental refresh, PySpark authoring, in-place updates, and data quality constraints. For more information, see [Get started with materialized lake views](../data-engineering/materialized-lake-views/get-started-with-materialized-lake-views.md).|
|March 2026|**Copilot context awareness for notebooks (Preview)**|The [updated Copilot for Data Engineering and Data Science (Preview)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/introducing-the-updated-copilot-for-data-engineering-and-data-science-preview?ft=All) provides built-in context awareness of your workspace, attached lakehouse schemas, notebook structure, and execution environment. Copilot can generate multi-step code, refactor existing logic, summarize complex notebooks, and diagnose failures with Fix with Copilot. For more information, see [Copilot for Data Engineering and Data Science](../data-engineering/copilot-notebooks-overview.md).|
|March 2026|**Private link support for API for GraphQL (Generally Available)**|[Private link support for API for GraphQL (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/34710?ft=All) enables tenant-level private endpoint connectivity for GraphQL APIs, ensuring data traffic flows through Microsoft's private backbone network for enhanced security and compliance. For more information, see [About Private Links for Secure Access to Fabric](../security/security-private-links-overview.md).|
|March 2026|**Fabric Runtime 2.0 (Preview)**|[Fabric Runtime 2.0 (Preview)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/fabric-runtime-2-0-preview?ft=All) includes Apache Spark 4.0, Delta Lake 4.0, Java 21, Scala 2.13, and Python 3.12 on Azure Linux 3.0, with upgrades to Spark 4.1, Delta Lake 4.1, and Python 3.13 coming soon. For more information, see [Fabric Runtime 2.0](../data-engineering/runtime-2-0.md) and [Apache Spark runtimes overview](../data-engineering/runtime.md).|
|March 2026|**Fabric notebook public APIs (Generally Available)**|[Fabric notebook public APIs (Generally Available)](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/fabric-notebook-public-apis-generally-available?ft=All) enable you to programmatically manage and execute notebooks with full CRUD support via the Items REST API and on-demand execution via the Job Scheduler API, including support for returning exit values from runs for conditional orchestration and signaling outcomes, with monitoring and cancellation of job instances, and service principal authentication. For more information, see [Items - REST API (Core)](/rest/api/fabric/core/items) and [Job Scheduler - REST API (Core)](/rest/api/fabric/core/job-scheduler).|

For more information, see [OneLake Security for SQL analytics endpoints](../onelake/sql-analytics-endpoint-onelake-security.md) and [OneLake security overview](../onelake/security/get-started-security.md).|
|October 2025|**OneLake security (Preview)**|[OneLake security](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/onelake-security-is-now-available-in-public-preview?ft=All), now a preview feature, is fine-grained access control for OneLake data, including folder, row, and column-level security. For more information, see [OneLake shortcut security](../onelake/onelake-shortcut-security.md) and [OneLake data access security API](/rest/api/fabric/core/onelake-data-access-security).|

For more information, see [Workspace outbound access protection](../security/workspace-outbound-access-protection-overview.md).|

#### Fabric Data Engineering samples and guidance

|**Month** | **Feature** |  **Learn more**|

This capability keeps OneLake as the source of truth while allowing Databricks compute to analyze tables through synchronized metadata and zero-copy data access. For more information, see [Enable OneLake catalog federation](/azure/databricks/query-federation/onelake).|
|February 2026|**Native Execution Engine for Microsoft Fabric**|[The Native Execution Engine](https://blog.fabric.microsoft.com/blog/under-the-hood-an-introduction-to-the-native-execution-engine-for-microsoft-fabric?ft=All) accelerates Spark jobs up to six times faster with no code changes by offloading compute-intensive operations to a vectorized C++ engine powered by Velox and Apache Gluten. It delivers improved throughput for Parquet and Delta workloads while maintaining full Spark compatibility. For more information, see [Native Execution Engine overview](../data-engineering/native-execution-engine-overview.md) and [Apache Spark advisor](../data-engineering/spark-advisor-introduction.md).|

By using this integration, you can discover streaming sources in Real-Time Hub, generate autogenerated PySpark code, reuse existing notebooks as processors, and connect securely by using Entra ID authentication. For more information, see [Microsoft Fabric Eventstreams Overview](../real-time-intelligence/event-streams/overview.md) and [How to use notebooks](../data-engineering/how-to-use-notebook.md).|

Fabric predicts demand and right-sizes starter pools so most notebook sessions start in seconds, falling back to on-demand when custom libraries or private networking are required.
